<review>Best egg tart in town. They increased the price by a quarter to $2.50 per egg tart, and $30 per dozen.

Moon cake is another popular item here. I personally like their pineapple moon cake with salty egg yolk.

They often takes months off, and if they open they usually open from noon to around 6 or 8pm, and off 2 days during weekdays.

Cash only!<//review>< Pics>

< Text>
This place is known for their flaky, delicious egg tarts and baked pastries. The crust for all their baked goods is buttery and phenomenal!  The negatives of this place include: long lines (need to wait at least 15-20 minutes before it's your turn), inconsistent operating hours (even though the door sign says 10am, sometimes they don't open until 11am; same with closing hours, sometimes they close at 3pm, 4pm, 5pm, other times they are just not open at all), egg tarts and the other baked goods are now $2.50 each (more expensive than the other bakeries).  The AA bakery around the corner of Jackson and Stockton (1068 stockton) has great egg tarts too, and it's only $1.25. Rather go there than Golden Gate, you dont need to wait in line, and they are always open.<//Text>

< review>
If you're looking for the famous custard egg tarts, do NOT trust the open and close hours listed on Google. They also randomly close, so the best way to catch these scrumptious tarts is to check first thing in the morning on the store's door if they've posted when the egg tarts will be available. Be careful, they may sell out quickly so don't delay!

The flaky, lightly sweet egg tarts are heavenly and if you are lucky enough to try it fresh, you may end up eating a whole box in one sitting! The price is a little more expensive compared to other Chinatown bakeries, but it is well worth it! A dozen (one pink box) is $30 or $2.50 for each individual tart.< /review>

<user>101150753919069824692< /user><Name>Chris Yu<//Name>< Time>
1535257752593< /Time>
<Rate>4< /Rate>< review>
I can't believe they're open for once! I've been flying up to the Bay area from LA quite frequently and they're always conveniently on vacation when I visit. I swear they do it on purpose but I'm glad I got to experience their famous egg tarts for once. Hailing from LA, we've got a lot of Hong Kong dim sum restaurants in the 626 but they can't compare to those up in SF. Historically, Chinese immigrants settled up north for the railroads before coming down to LA and I feel like those ancestors established different Chinese cuisine than those down in LA. Not only does it taste different, the people who make them are different.

Enough with the history lesson, let's get down to business. The egg tarts here has a flaky crust all around and an extremely hot core when you take your first bite. I have never tasted any egg tart fresh off the oven and straight into my mouth. For a box of 12, $30 may seem steep but it's worth it. I can see why the business owners take so many vacations throughout the year. You must try this place out of your ever in SF and only if they're open, which usually is 50/50.</review>

<Name>Jason Riddell<//Name>< text>
Was walking through Chinatown on a Sunday and saw a queue, the head of which was outside the Golden Gate Bakery, I had heard of them and decided to join the queue as it was pure luck I was there when it was open as the opening times are random and they close up for months at a time for vacation. The 30 minutes wait was well worth it the egg tarts were amazing, the coconut cookies great, and the sesame seed bun good too. Egg tarts are $2.50 each but as a treat worth it. They only take cash but there are a couple of banks over the road so no big deal.< /text>

< Review>
I visited between lunch and dinner on a Wednesday afternoon. It wasn't very busy when I walked up and I lucked out because they still had warm egg tarts. At $2.50 apiece they're more expensive than I'm accustomed to but they are well worth the price. As far as I know, egg tarts typically have crusts similar to pie crusts or flaky crusts. The Golden Gate Bakery egg tarts have flaky crusts but the layers are so tightly packed I thought they were like a pie crust at first sight. The layers are buttery and savory which pairs well with the eggy, silky smooth custard. I only bought 2 but next time I'm in town, I'm buying many more.< /Review>

<Review>Been coming here for many years - never once have I seen this place without a line. Okay, maybe once.. but that was because they were closed for vacation / holidays (rarely happens). There is a good reason for that - this is probably the best egg tart you're going to have, counting Asia. They are the best fresh so my recommendation is to eat right after you get it while they are still hot. They have other stuff as well (wife cakes, lotus seed buns, etc) but those are definitely less amazing than the egg tarts.

PSA: This place is cash only. Make sure you have some!< /Review><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< resp>

< Text>
There always seems to be a line, but I think it's worth it! I passed by the bakery about 10 minutes before it opened at noon on a Saturday, and the line was short enough at the time, so I thought to try it out. The custard tarts are $2.50 per piece ($30 per dozen in a box). They're freshly baked as some had to wait a few minutes as they were ordering a dozen (I only wanted to try two pieces, so they let me have the two). It's flaky, creamy and really delicious! Cash only at this place, like most places in Chinatown it seems.< /Text>

<Rate>4<//Rate><text>Best eggtart in San Francisco hands down...if you're willing to wait. The line, on weekends, will run you about 45 minutes, but if you've never tried their eggtarts, or if you're in need for your eggtart fix, it's well worth it. They have the perfect blend of flakiness in their crust and milky creaminess in their filling. How do they do it??? I've never had another eggtart as good as GG Bakery...doesn't make sense! Well, that's why there is a line and that's why there is a wait. The server and cashier is pretty rude though, you can tell they don't want to be there. And that is true a lot of times. If you're making a trip out here specifically to get their eggtarts or other baked goods, make sure to call them, or find out someway somehow, if they are open. They tend to go on vacation PRETTY OFTEN. Not even kidding. I guess when you've made a transcending recipe like that and become rich you'd take as many vacations as them as well. Egg tarts are a little on the pricey side too, of course, at just about $2/pc and $24/dozen. Their red bean sesame balls are pretty legit as well and their wifey cookies are good if they have them available.</text>< pics>

<user_id>102369733394698345145</user_id>< Name>
Stephanie Moris</Name>
<Date>1566308116587</Date>< Rating>
4< /Rating>
<Text>Yet again, Yelp successfully led me to a business with exactly what I was looking for: exceptionally delicious, freshly baked egg tarts.

Buying a dozen of the egg tarts at Golden Gate Bakery will set you back $30 in cold, hard cash; they accept cash only! The cost is currently $2.50 per tart.

I stepped into a line with about 15 people ahead of me, thinking the wait should not take more than 30 minutes. I was very wrong.  I realized about a half an hour in that I had only moved up in line because some people had lost hope and abandoned their quest for egg tarts. Since I had waited for some time already, I continued to stand in line as people constantly stared quizzically at the line as they walked and drove by.  Many passersby asked what we were waiting for and asked if the business was even open.

I understood why people kept thinking the bakery was closed. They have an interesting set up: one lady unlocks the bakery entrance door, pokes her head out, takes your order and your cash, closes and locks the door behind her, places the egg tarts into a box, one at a time, and unlocks the door once more to hand you your order. It is as if those egg tarts are kept more secure than money in a bank (kidding, somewhat...I'm sure their huge profits must need to be guarded as well).

This really was the best egg tart I have ever had. At other bakeries, the crust can be flavorless, but the crust on these were flakey and buttery. The tradeoff for these freshly baked egg tarts is the large quantity of time it takes them to prep one person's order. It seems like they could only fill a couple of people's orders at a time before having to wait another 20 minutes for the next batch to be ready.< /Text>< Pictures>
None<//Pictures>

<rating>5< /rating>< Text>
This place was insanely unique. With the bread factory right next door to the restaurant and windows looking in to see the bakers at work. When you go up to the counter to order your food, you can see a conveyor belt with baskets hanging on the ceiling, carrying loaves of freshly baked bread throughout the place. There is a gift shop and a separate counter just for buying their bread creations. It is usually bustling with activity, being right next to the bay and in the center of a popular tourist area. A little pricey but nearly everything is a little more expensive in San Fran. Very enjoyable and good food< /Text>

<Date>1488623819654< /Date>< text>
The custard tarts here are to die for! No other place even comes close. The only downside to this place is that the location is always difficult to drive in and parking is horrendous. If you're local and/or don't mind taking the bus, this place is great.

For me, I HAVE to eat these custard tarts on the spot. I don't like them after they have cooled down. So, I usually only just buy one or two. My other friends typically buy a dozen or so. The prices are slightly more expensive from what I remember as well. About $2/each.

And there is usually a line. So be prepared to not only struggle to find parking, but to wait for your yummy tarts.</text>

<user_id>103648869939034149670</user_id><username>Winson Wong<//username><time>1403731783972<//time>< Rating>
4< /Rating>
<Text>So I have mixed feelings about Golden Gate Bakery and their Egg Custard Tarts. I think I just have too high expectations of the place. Everyone talks about it and I had it, it was really good. The pastry was crispy and the custard was perfectly done, tender not too runny and yet not too bouncy like gelatin texture either. Eat the tart when it comes out of the oven, I was lucky to get that, it's the perfect temperature and makes you feel all warm and fuzzy inside. I tried their other stuff like banana cake etc, they were decent, not spectacular but pretty good.

However, what I don't like about it, which I can't really put my hands on it but the flavor is different to what a traditional Hong Kong egg custard tart should taste. I can't explain it, it's just different. They're both very good but I think I just had an expectation that it would be more traditional.< /Text>< Pics>

< Review>
This place is known for their egg tarts, people will stand in line waiting for them to come out of the oven.  The lines can be long and people will order boxes of these egg tarts.  The down side, they are very pricey compared to the other shops.  Yes the other shops may not be as good, but you won't have to wait in line.  They also have the standard BBQ pork buns and other sweets, but everyone comes here for the egg tar. This bakery has the strangest operating hours ever. It doesn't matter because their egg tarts are so good that you'll be at their mercy anyway! <Text>The egg tarts are a must get!!! Whenever I'm in the city, I try to make a trip to Chinatown just to get these addicting desserts. The shop is like most shops in Chinatown with an unattractive exterior to match its interior. There is only a small cramped space in front of the counter for you to place your order. The egg tarts are now $1.50 each (Cash only), which is a pricey. However, considering how I've very had egg tarts this delicious, the price is justified. The egg tarts are larger than your average egg tart and are always hot and fresh when I have ordered them. People say that there's always a long wait, but I've never experienced this since I probably come during off times. <UserId.>103748551017913986634< /UserId.><Name>Col Chong<//Name>< time>
1517353083671< /time>
< rating>
5< /rating>
< review>
This place way exceeded my expectations. With alllll the hype, I was pretty skeptical but now I see. I actually burned the inside of my mouth eating that egg tart, but I don't even care. If I could give 7 stars, I'd give that egg tart 7 stars out of 5.

I also got a wintermelon pastry to see if this place is just good for egg tarts. I bought it, didn't eat it (was too overwhelmed by egg tart), put it in the fridge, and took a bite the next morning. It was....amazing. The best wintermelon pastry I've had and I've had a lot of them. And this wasn't even fresh, and I was too lazy to microwave it so it was COLD. And it still tasted like heaven. There were wintermelon bits and almond bits in the filling that gave a really nice and fun texture. It was just perfect.
[EDIT] I microwaved the rest and it tasted even more amazing if that's even possible.

If I could create magical pastries like these, I'd take 5-6 months off every year too.</review>

<text>We came here with our friends on a Sat night. After knowing they don't take reservation and usually have a line, we came right before 5PM. Luckily, that turned out to be perfect timing. We only waited about 5 minutes before being seated. Strangely, a lot of people were already eating and I was not sure if they were eating dinner or a late lunch?

At any rate, we had buffet dinner at $24 a person. A child over 4 is charged like half of the price. They have an interesting rule of ordering no more than 4 meat at the same time. You can, however, order other dishes as often as you like including tofu soup, fried chicken, etc. Their beverage prices are quite reasonable too although I didn't waste my appetite on drinks. My favorite is their kalbi, bulgogi and beef tip. They have free bonchons (kimchi, potato salad, etc.) but no typical Korean steamed eggs or seafood pancake. I personally think that is a miss.

One thing to note and perhaps to improve is their fan system for seats by the windows. Essentially, there is no fan so those seats get a lot of smoke and that means your clothes will smell like Korean BBQ :)

Last but not the least is their customer service is very good and friendly. I actually lost my sunglasses at the seat because my son was going through my bag. Fortunately, I left them a message on FB and the manager was able to find it for me. Will be back for this place!<//text>< Pictures>

<date>1383203869917<//date><Text>4 stars for the egg tarts here but after trying the over-priced moon cakes here, I had to give it just 3 stars.

Honestly, I don‚Äôt even know why I stood in that dreadful line at Golden Gate bakery because I absolutely hated moon cakes as a child and have stayed away from them ever since. The line was only exacerbated by the fact that Mid-Autumn Festival was coming up that weekend, and China Town was overflowing with festivities. For those not privy to Chinese holidays, Mid-Autumn Festival is a big deal. Back home in Taiwan, my parents, my little sister, and our whole extended family spend a whole weekend BBQing, eating moon cakes, peeling pomelos, and moon gazing together. Gifting beautifully designed boxes of moon cakes to friends and family was common, stealthily re-gifting these boxes was also not uncommon.

Out of nostalgia, I decided to give moon cakes another try. The fact that I just happened to be a few blocks away from the ever-so-popular Golden Gate Bakery that day gave me another reason to swing by.

<user>100864918851588063967</user><Name>Tina Chan Ling</Name>< time>
1394576043939</time>
< Rating>
3< /Rating>
< Text>
Local tiny mom and pop bakery shop located in Chinatown serving up what people call the best "dan tat" or egg custard tarts around town. It has definitely become a tourist attraction but you'll find some locals here as well. I will say the egg tarts were pretty darn good one or two years ago but I've noticed either the recipe or baker has changed since the crust is not as flaky and buttery as before. It's a bit overpriced at over $1 per egg tart but is still a great snack for those who have never tried one before.

Be prepared for long lines and bundle up since the wait can be up to an hour long at times. There aren't any tables available to sit and eat at either. Workers here aren't the friendliest and they don't speak much English so if all fails just point to what you want through the glass case.<//Text>

<userid>100249539677162904250< /userid><text>I guess Golden Gate Bakery doesn't really need my help in recommending them, but I have to say that their egg tarts are really good. You MUST eat them fresh to enjoy their flaky, eggy goodness. Otherwise, they get exponentially worse with every minute you wait to eat them.

That said, a fresh GGB egg tart has a delicate, flaky crust. Each layer is really thin and provides a very enjoyable light crisp as your teeth sink into it. The custard is smooth with a semi-gelatinous jiggly texture, and its flavor is pleasantly eggy and sweet but not overtly buttery or rich.  I like that it's not too rich, buttery, or heavy as the crust's relative lightness compliments the sweet egg custard perfectly! These delectable treats are the only reasons you need to take a trip to Chinatown. Yes, reasons, because you won't just eat one.

I also want to add that I only find these lighter, sweeter egg tarts around here. Whenever I've been to Hong Kong or Macau, they tend to be richer and heavier but still very delicious. If you want to try an egg tart that resembles that kind of style, order the Portuguese Tarts (Po Tat) from Koi Palace. They have a thicker, richer crust while the egg custard is more buttery and heavier. They're much more decadent if that's your thing. I can't get enough of either!</text>< user_name>
Nei Ng< /user_name>
